<p><b>Bavaria</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;v&#39; in &#39;vie&#39;">v</span><span title="/ɛər/: &#39;are&#39; in &#39;bare&#39;">ɛər</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_language" title="Bavarian language">Bavarian</a>: <i>Bayern</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈbaɪɐn]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>: <i lang="cs">Bavorsko</i>), officially the <b>Free State of Bavaria</b> (German and Bavarian: <i>Freistaat Bayern</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈfʁaɪʃtaːt ˈbaɪɐn]</a></span>), is a landlocked <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">federal state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Germany">Germany</a>, occupying its southeastern corner. With an area of 70,550.19 square kilometres (27,200 sq mi), Bavaria is the largest German state by land area comprising roughly a fifth of the total land area of Germany. With 13&#160;million inhabitants, it is Germany's second-most-populous state after <a href="/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia" title="North Rhine-Westphalia">North Rhine-Westphalia</a>. Bavaria's main cities are <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> (its capital and largest city and also the third <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_by_population" title="List of cities in Germany by population">largest city in Germany</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bavaria" title="History of Bavaria">history of Bavaria</a> includes its earliest settlement by <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> tribes, followed by the conquests of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> in the 1st century BC, when the territory was incorporated into the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Raetia" title="Raetia">Raetia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Noricum" title="Noricum">Noricum</a>. It became a <a href="/wiki/Stem_duchy" title="Stem duchy">stem duchy</a> in the 6th century AD following the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>. It was later incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, became an independent kingdom, joined the Prussian-led <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> in 1871 while retaining its title of kingdom, and finally became a <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">state</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Germany">Federal Republic of Germany</a> in 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria" title="Duchy of Bavaria">Duchy of Bavaria</a> dates back to the year 555. In the 17th century AD, the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Bavaria">Duke of Bavaria</a> became a <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">Prince-elector</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">Kingdom of Bavaria</a> existed from 1806 to 1918, when Bavaria became a republic. In 1946, the Free State of Bavaria reorganized itself on democratic lines after the Second World War.
</p><p>Bavaria has a unique culture, largely because of the state's former <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> majority and conservative traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-EKD2016_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EKD2016-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bavarian people">Bavarians</a> have traditionally been proud of their culture, which includes a <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_language" title="Bavarian language">language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_cuisine" title="Bavarian cuisine">cuisine</a>, architecture, festivals such as <a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">Oktoberfest</a> and elements of <a href="/wiki/The_Alps" class="mw-redirect" title="The Alps">Alpine</a> symbolism.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The state also has the second largest economy among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_states_by_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="List of German states by GDP">German states by GDP figures</a>, giving it a status as a rather wealthy German region.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Modern Bavaria also includes parts of the historical regions of <a href="/wiki/Franconia" title="Franconia">Franconia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabia</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Bavarians emerged in a region north of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>, previously inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>, which had been part of the Roman provinces of <a href="/wiki/Raetia" title="Raetia">Raetia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Noricum" title="Noricum">Noricum</a>. The Bavarians spoke <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a>, but, unlike other Germanic groups, they probably did not migrate from elsewhere. Rather, they seem to have coalesced out of other groups left behind by the Roman withdrawal late in the 5th century. These peoples may have included the Celtic <a href="/wiki/Boii" title="Boii">Boii</a>, some remaining <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marcomanni" title="Marcomanni">Marcomanni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allemanni" class="mw-redirect" title="Allemanni">Allemanni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quadi" title="Quadi">Quadi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thuringians" class="mw-redirect" title="Thuringians">Thuringians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scirians" class="mw-redirect" title="Scirians">Scirians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugians" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugians">Rugians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heruli" class="mw-redirect" title="Heruli">Heruli</a>. The name "Bavarian" ("<a href="/wiki/Baiuvarii" class="mw-redirect" title="Baiuvarii">Baiuvarii</a>") means "Men of Baia" which may indicate Bohemia, the homeland of the Celtic <a href="/wiki/Boii" title="Boii">Boii</a> and later of the Marcomanni. They first appear in written sources circa 520. A 17th century Jewish chronicler <a href="/wiki/David_Gans" title="David Gans">David Solomon Ganz</a>, citing <a href="/wiki/Cyriacus_Spangenberg" title="Cyriacus Spangenberg">Cyriacus Spangenberg</a>, claimed that the diocese was named after an ancient Bohemian king, Boiia, in the 14th century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-ganz_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ganz-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria" title="Duchy of Bavaria">Duchy of Bavaria</a></div>
<p>From about 554 to 788, the house of <a href="/wiki/Agilolfing" class="mw-redirect" title="Agilolfing">Agilolfing</a> ruled the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria" title="Duchy of Bavaria">Duchy of Bavaria</a>, ending with <a href="/wiki/Tassilo_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Tassilo III">Tassilo III</a> who was deposed by <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Three early dukes are named in <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> sources: <a href="/wiki/Garibald_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Garibald I">Garibald I</a> may have been appointed to the office by the <a href="/wiki/Merovingian" class="mw-redirect" title="Merovingian">Merovingian</a> kings and married the <a href="/wiki/Lombardy" title="Lombardy">Lombard</a> princess Walderada when the church forbade her to King <a href="/wiki/Chlothar_I" title="Chlothar I">Chlothar I</a> in 555. Their daughter, <a href="/wiki/Theodelinde" class="mw-redirect" title="Theodelinde">Theodelinde</a>, became Queen of the Lombards in northern Italy and Garibald was forced to flee to her when he fell out with his Frankish overlords. Garibald's successor, <a href="/wiki/Tassilo_I_of_Bavaria" title="Tassilo I of Bavaria">Tassilo I</a>, tried unsuccessfully to hold the eastern frontier against the expansion of <a href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic peoples">Slavs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avars</a> around 600. Tassilo's son <a href="/wiki/Garibald_II_of_Bavaria" title="Garibald II of Bavaria">Garibald II</a> seems to have achieved a balance of power between 610 and 616.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Garibald II little is known of the Bavarians until <a href="/wiki/Theodo_of_Bavaria#Ordinals" title="Theodo of Bavaria">Duke Theodo I</a>, whose reign may have begun as early as 680. From 696 onward, he invited churchmen from the west to organize churches and strengthen Christianity in his duchy. (It is unclear what Bavarian religious life consisted of before this time.) His son, <a href="/wiki/Theodbert_of_Bavaria" title="Theodbert of Bavaria">Theudebert</a>, led a decisive Bavarian campaign to intervene in a succession dispute in the <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">Lombard Kingdom</a> in 714, and married his sister Guntrud to the Lombard <a href="/wiki/Liutprand,_King_of_the_Lombards" title="Liutprand, King of the Lombards">King Liutprand</a>. At Theodo's death the duchy was divided among his sons, but reunited under his grandson <a href="/wiki/Hugbert_of_Bavaria" title="Hugbert of Bavaria">Hugbert</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baiern_unter_den_Carolingern_im_Jahre_900.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Baiern_unter_den_Carolingern_im_Jahre_900.jpg/220px-Baiern_unter_den_Carolingern_im_Jahre_900.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Baiern_unter_den_Carolingern_im_Jahre_900.jpg/330px-Baiern_unter_den_Carolingern_im_Jahre_900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Baiern_unter_den_Carolingern_im_Jahre_900.jpg/440px-Baiern_unter_den_Carolingern_im_Jahre_900.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2953" data-file-height="2362" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baiern_unter_den_Carolingern_im_Jahre_900.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Kingdom of Bavaria in 900</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Karte_Herzogtum_Bayern_im_10._Jahrhundert.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Karte_Herzogtum_Bayern_im_10._Jahrhundert.png/220px-Karte_Herzogtum_Bayern_im_10._Jahrhundert.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Karte_Herzogtum_Bayern_im_10._Jahrhundert.png/330px-Karte_Herzogtum_Bayern_im_10._Jahrhundert.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Karte_Herzogtum_Bayern_im_10._Jahrhundert.png/440px-Karte_Herzogtum_Bayern_im_10._Jahrhundert.png 2x" data-file-width="2844" data-file-height="3008" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Karte_Herzogtum_Bayern_im_10._Jahrhundert.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bavaria in the 10th century</div></div></div>
<p>At Hugbert's death (735) the duchy passed to a distant relative named <a href="/wiki/Odilo_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Odilo of Bavaria">Odilo</a>, from neighboring <a href="/wiki/Alemannia" class="mw-redirect" title="Alemannia">Alemannia</a> (modern southwest Germany and northern Switzerland). Odilo issued a <a href="/wiki/Lex_Baiuvariorum" title="Lex Baiuvariorum">law code for Bavaria</a>, completed the process of church organization in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Saint_Boniface" title="Saint Boniface">St. Boniface</a> (739), and tried to intervene in Frankish succession disputes by fighting for the claims of the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_dynasty" title="Carolingian dynasty">Carolingian</a> <a href="/wiki/Grifo" title="Grifo">Grifo</a>. He was defeated near <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a> in 743 but continued to rule until his death in 748.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saint_Boniface" title="Saint Boniface">Saint Boniface</a> completed the people's conversion to Christianity in the early 8th century.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tassilo_III_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Tassilo III of Bavaria">Tassilo III</a> (b. 741 – d. after 796) succeeded his father at the age of eight after an unsuccessful attempt by Grifo to rule Bavaria. He initially ruled under Frankish oversight but began to function independently from 763 onward. He was particularly noted for founding new monasteries and for expanding eastwards, fighting Slavs in the eastern Alps and along the <a href="/wiki/River_Danube" class="mw-redirect" title="River Danube">River Danube</a> and colonizing these lands. After 781, however, his cousin Charlemagne began to pressure Tassilo to submit and finally deposed him in 788. The deposition was not entirely legitimate. Dissenters attempted a coup against Charlemagne at Tassilo's old capital of <a href="/wiki/Regensburg" title="Regensburg">Regensburg</a> in 792, led by his own son <a href="/wiki/Pepin_the_Hunchback" title="Pepin the Hunchback">Pépin the Hunchback</a>. The king had to drag Tassilo out of imprisonment to formally renounce his rights and titles at the Assembly of Frankfurt in 794. This is the last appearance of Tassilo in the sources, and he probably died a monk. As all of his family were also forced into monasteries, this was the end of the Agilolfing dynasty.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayern_nach_der_Teilung_1392.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Bayern_nach_der_Teilung_1392.png/220px-Bayern_nach_der_Teilung_1392.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Bayern_nach_der_Teilung_1392.png/330px-Bayern_nach_der_Teilung_1392.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Bayern_nach_der_Teilung_1392.png/440px-Bayern_nach_der_Teilung_1392.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1196" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayern_nach_der_Teilung_1392.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bavarian duchies after the partition of 1392</div></div></div>
<p>For the next 400 years numerous families held the duchy, rarely for more than three generations. With the revolt of duke <a href="/wiki/Henry_II,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="Henry II, Duke of Bavaria">Henry the Quarrelsome</a> in 976, Bavaria lost large territories in the south and south east. The territory of <i><a href="/wiki/Name_of_Austria" title="Name of Austria">Ostarrichi</a></i> was elevated to a duchy in its own right and given to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Babenberg" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Babenberg">Babenberger family</a>. This event marks the founding of <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>.
</p><p>The last, and one of the most important, of the dukes of Bavaria was <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Lion" title="Henry the Lion">Henry the Lion</a> of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Welf" title="House of Welf">house of Welf</a>, founder of Munich, and <i>de facto</i> the second most powerful man in the empire as the ruler of two duchies. When in 1180, Henry the Lion was deposed as Duke of <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">Saxony</a> and Bavaria by his cousin, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick I, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick I, Holy Roman Emperor</a> (a.k.a. "Barbarossa" for his red beard), Bavaria was awarded as <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fief</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Wittelsbach" class="mw-redirect" title="Wittelsbach">Wittelsbach</a> family, counts palatinate of Schyren ("Scheyern" in modern German). They ruled for 738 years, from 1180 to 1918. The <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_the_Palatinate" class="mw-redirect" title="Electorate of the Palatinate">Electorate of the Palatinate</a> by Rhine (<i>Kurpfalz</i> in German) was also acquired by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wittelsbach" title="House of Wittelsbach">House of Wittelsbach</a> in 1214, which they would subsequently hold for six centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first of several divisions of the duchy of Bavaria occurred in 1255. With the extinction of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hohenstaufen" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Hohenstaufen">Hohenstaufen</a> in 1268, <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabian</a> territories were acquired by the Wittelsbach dukes. <a href="/wiki/Louis_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Louis IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Louis the Bavarian</a> acquired <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tyrol" title="County of Tyrol">Tyrol</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Holland" title="County of Holland">Holland</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_of_Hainaut" title="County of Hainaut">Hainaut</a> for his House but released the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Palatinate" title="Upper Palatinate">Upper Palatinate</a> for the Palatinate branch of the Wittelsbach in 1329. In the 14th and 15th centuries, upper and lower Bavaria were repeatedly subdivided. Four Duchies existed after the division of 1392: <a href="/wiki/Bavaria-Straubing" title="Bavaria-Straubing">Bavaria-Straubing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bavaria-Landshut" title="Bavaria-Landshut">Bavaria-Landshut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bavaria-Ingolstadt" title="Bavaria-Ingolstadt">Bavaria-Ingolstadt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bavaria-Munich" title="Bavaria-Munich">Bavaria-Munich</a>.  In 1506 with the <a href="/wiki/Landshut_War_of_Succession" class="mw-redirect" title="Landshut War of Succession">Landshut War of Succession</a>, the other parts of Bavaria were reunited, and Munich became the sole capital. The country became one of the Jesuit-supported counter-reformation centers. 
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:J%C3%B6rg_R%C3%BCgen_(ca_1510).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/J%C3%B6rg_R%C3%BCgen_%28ca_1510%29.jpg/180px-J%C3%B6rg_R%C3%BCgen_%28ca_1510%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/J%C3%B6rg_R%C3%BCgen_%28ca_1510%29.jpg/270px-J%C3%B6rg_R%C3%BCgen_%28ca_1510%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/J%C3%B6rg_R%C3%BCgen_%28ca_1510%29.jpg/360px-J%C3%B6rg_R%C3%BCgen_%28ca_1510%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="658" data-file-height="950" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:J%C3%B6rg_R%C3%BCgen_(ca_1510).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bavarian <a href="/wiki/Herald" title="Herald">herald</a> Joerg Rugenn wearing a <a href="/wiki/Tabard" title="Tabard">tabard</a> of the arms around 1510</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electorate_of_Bavaria">Electorate of Bavaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Electorate of Bavaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Bavaria" title="Electorate of Bavaria">Electorate of Bavaria</a></div>
<p>In 1623 the Bavarian duke replaced his relative of the Palatinate branch, the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_the_Palatinate" class="mw-redirect" title="Electorate of the Palatinate">Electorate of the Palatinate</a> in the early days of the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years&#39; War">Thirty Years' War</a> and acquired the powerful <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">prince-electoral</a> dignity in the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, determining its Emperor thence forward, as well as special legal status under the empire's laws. 
</p><p>During the early and mid-18th century the ambitions of the Bavarian prince electors led to several wars with Austria as well as occupations by Austria (<a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> with the election of a Wittelsbach emperor instead of a Habsburg). From 1777 onward, and after the younger Bavarian branch of the family had died out with elector <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_III_Joseph,_Elector_of_Bavaria" title="Maximilian III Joseph, Elector of Bavaria">Max III Joseph</a>, Bavaria and the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_the_Palatinate" class="mw-redirect" title="Electorate of the Palatinate">Electorate of the Palatinate</a> were governed once again in <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a>, now by the Palatinian lines. The new state also comprised the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_J%C3%BClich" title="Duchy of Jülich">Duchies of Jülich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berg_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Berg (state)">Berg</a> as these on their part were in personal union with the Palatinate.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Bavaria">Kingdom of Bavaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Bavaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">Kingdom of Bavaria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayern_von_1800_bis_heute.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Bayern_von_1800_bis_heute.png/220px-Bayern_von_1800_bis_heute.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Bayern_von_1800_bis_heute.png/330px-Bayern_von_1800_bis_heute.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e1/Bayern_von_1800_bis_heute.png 2x" data-file-width="422" data-file-height="385" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayern_von_1800_bis_heute.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bavaria in the 19th century and beyond</div></div></div>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> abolished the Holy Roman Empire, Bavaria became a <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">kingdom</a> in 1806 due, in part, to the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">Confederation of the Rhine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Its area doubled after the Duchy of Jülich was ceded to France, as the Electoral Palatinate was divided between France and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Baden" title="Grand Duchy of Baden">Grand Duchy of Baden</a>. The Duchy of Berg was given to <a href="/wiki/Jerome_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerome Bonaparte">Jerome Bonaparte</a>. The <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tyrol" title="County of Tyrol">Tyrol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salzburg_(state)" title="Salzburg (state)">Salzburg</a> were temporarily reunited with Bavaria but finally ceded to Austria by the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>.  In return Bavaria was allowed to annex the modern-day region of <a href="/wiki/Palatinate_(region)" title="Palatinate (region)">Palatinate</a> to the west of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franconia" title="Franconia">Franconia</a> in 1815.  Between 1799 and 1817, the leading minister, Count <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Joseph_von_Montgelas" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximilian Joseph von Montgelas">Montgelas</a>, followed a strict policy of modernisation; he laid the foundations of administrative structures that survived the monarchy and retain core validity in the 21st century. In May 1808 a first constitution was passed by <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I_Joseph_of_Bavaria" title="Maximilian I Joseph of Bavaria">Maximilian I</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> being modernized in 1818. This second version established a bicameral Parliament with a House of Lords (<i>Kammer der Reichsräte</i>) and a House of Commons (<i>Kammer der Abgeordneten</i>). That constitution was followed until the collapse of the monarchy at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.
</p><p>After the rise of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a> to power in the early 18th century, Bavaria preserved its independence by playing off the rivalry of Prussia and <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austria</a>. Allied to Austria, it was defeated along with Austrian in the 1866 <a href="/wiki/Austro-Prussian_War" title="Austro-Prussian War">Austro-Prussian War</a> and was not incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/North_German_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="North German Federation">North German Confederation</a> of 1867, but the question of German unity was still alive. When <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">France declared war on Prussia in 1870</a>, the south German states Baden, Württemberg, Hessen-Darmstadt and Bavaria joined the Prussian forces (whereas Austria did not) and ultimately joined the Federation, which was renamed <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire"><i>Deutsches Reich</i> (German Empire)</a> in 1871 while Austria did not. Bavaria continued as a monarchy, and it had some special rights within the federation (such as an army, railways, postal service and a diplomatic body of its own).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Part_of_the_German_Empire">Part of the German Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Part of the German Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Block_of_Bavarian_stamps_(1920s)_overprinted_with_%22Deutsches_Reich%22.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Block_of_Bavarian_stamps_%281920s%29_overprinted_with_%22Deutsches_Reich%22.jpg/170px-Block_of_Bavarian_stamps_%281920s%29_overprinted_with_%22Deutsches_Reich%22.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Block_of_Bavarian_stamps_%281920s%29_overprinted_with_%22Deutsches_Reich%22.jpg/255px-Block_of_Bavarian_stamps_%281920s%29_overprinted_with_%22Deutsches_Reich%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/49/Block_of_Bavarian_stamps_%281920s%29_overprinted_with_%22Deutsches_Reich%22.jpg 2x" data-file-width="327" data-file-height="380" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Block_of_Bavarian_stamps_(1920s)_overprinted_with_%22Deutsches_Reich%22.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bavarian stamps during the German Empire</div></div></div>
<p>When Bavaria became part of the newly formed German Empire, this action was considered controversial by <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_nationalism" title="Bavarian nationalism">Bavarian nationalists</a> who had wanted to retain independence from the rest of Germany, as Austria had. As Bavaria had a majority-Catholic population, many people resented being ruled by the mostly <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> northerners of <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>. As a direct result of the Bavarian-Prussian feud, political parties formed to encourage Bavaria to break away and regain its independence.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan2000_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan2000-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Although the idea of Bavarian separatism was popular in the late 19th and early 20th century, apart from a small minority such as the <a href="/wiki/Bavaria_Party" title="Bavaria Party">Bavaria Party</a>, most Bavarians accepted that Bavaria is part of Germany.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In the early 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Wassily_Kandinsky" title="Wassily Kandinsky">Wassily Kandinsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Klee" title="Paul Klee">Paul Klee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Ibsen" title="Henrik Ibsen">Henrik Ibsen</a>, and other artists were drawn to Bavaria, especially to the <a href="/wiki/Schwabing" title="Schwabing">Schwabing</a> district of Munich, a center of international artistic activity. This area was devastated by bombing and invasion during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_State_of_Bavaria">Free State of Bavaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Free State of Bavaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kriegerdenkmal_Dietelskirchen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Kriegerdenkmal_Dietelskirchen.jpg/130px-Kriegerdenkmal_Dietelskirchen.jpg" decoding="async" width="130" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Kriegerdenkmal_Dietelskirchen.jpg/195px-Kriegerdenkmal_Dietelskirchen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Kriegerdenkmal_Dietelskirchen.jpg/260px-Kriegerdenkmal_Dietelskirchen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2816" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kriegerdenkmal_Dietelskirchen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A memorial to soldiers who died in the two World Wars in Dietelskirchen, Bavaria</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dachau_Memorial_(iron_sculpture).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Dachau_Memorial_%28iron_sculpture%29.JPG/130px-Dachau_Memorial_%28iron_sculpture%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="130" height="85" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Dachau_Memorial_%28iron_sculpture%29.JPG/195px-Dachau_Memorial_%28iron_sculpture%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Dachau_Memorial_%28iron_sculpture%29.JPG/260px-Dachau_Memorial_%28iron_sculpture%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dachau_Memorial_(iron_sculpture).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dachau_concentration_camp" title="Dachau concentration camp">Dachau concentration camp</a> memorial sculpture erected in 1968</div></div></div>
<p><i>Free State</i> has been an adopted designation after the abolition of monarchy in the aftermath of World War I in several German states.
On 12 November 1918, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_III_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig III of Bavaria">Ludwig III</a> signed a document, the <a href="/wiki/Anif_declaration" title="Anif declaration">Anif declaration</a>, releasing both civil and military officers from their oaths; the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_State_of_Bavaria" title="People&#39;s State of Bavaria">newly formed republican government</a>, or "People's State" of Socialist premier <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Eisner" title="Kurt Eisner">Kurt Eisner</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> interpreted this as an abdication. To date, however, no member of the House of Wittelsbach has ever formally declared renunciation of the throne.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> On the other hand, none has ever since officially called upon their Bavarian or Stuart claims. Family members are active in cultural and social life, including the head of the house, <a href="/wiki/Franz,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="Franz, Duke of Bavaria">Franz, Duke of Bavaria</a>. They step back from any announcements on public affairs, showing approval or disapproval solely by Franz's presence or absence.
</p><p>Eisner was assassinated in February 1919, ultimately leading to a Communist revolt and the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Soviet_Republic" title="Bavarian Soviet Republic">Bavarian Soviet Republic</a> being proclaimed 6 April 1919. After violent suppression by elements of the German Army and notably the <a href="/wiki/Freikorps" title="Freikorps">Freikorps</a>, the Bavarian Soviet Republic fell in May 1919. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bavaria" title="Constitution of Bavaria">Bamberg Constitution</a> (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Bamberger Verfassung</i></i>) was enacted on 12 or 14 August 1919 and came into force on 15 September 1919 creating the Free State of Bavaria within the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a>. Extremist activity further increased, notably the 1923 <a href="/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="Beer Hall Putsch">Beer Hall Putsch</a> led by the <a href="/wiki/NSDAP" class="mw-redirect" title="NSDAP">National Socialists</a>, and Munich and Nuremberg became seen as <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> strongholds under the <a href="/wiki/Third_Reich" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a> of <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>. However, in the crucial <a href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_March_1933" class="mw-redirect" title="German federal election, March 1933">German federal election, March 1933</a>, the Nazis received less than 50% of the votes cast in Bavaria.
</p><p>As a manufacturing centre, Munich was heavily bombed during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and was occupied by U.S. troops, becoming a major part of the American Zone of <a href="/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany" title="Allied-occupied Germany">Allied-occupied Germany</a> (1945–47) and then of <a href="/wiki/Bizone" title="Bizone">"Bizonia"</a>.
</p><p>The Rhenish Palatinate was detached from Bavaria in 1946 and made part of the new state <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, Bavaria was part of <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>. In 1949, the Free State of Bavaria chose not to sign the Founding Treaty (<i>Gründungsvertrag</i>) for the formation of the Federal Republic of Germany, opposing the division of Germany into two states, after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Landtag_of_Bavaria" title="Landtag of Bavaria">Bavarian Parliament</a> did not sign the <a href="/wiki/Basic_Law_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Basic Law of Germany">Basic Law of Germany</a>, mainly because it was seen as not granting sufficient powers to the individual <i>Länder</i>, but at the same time decided that it would still come into force in Bavaria if two-thirds of the other <i>Länder</i> ratified it. All of the other <i>Länder</i> ratified it, and so it became law.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bavarian_identity">Bavarian identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Bavarian identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bavarians have often emphasized a separate national identity and considered themselves as "Bavarians" first, "Germans" second.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> This feeling started to come about more strongly among Bavarians when the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">Kingdom of Bavaria</a> joined the Protestant Prussian-dominated <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> while the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_nationalism" title="Bavarian nationalism">Bavarian nationalists</a> wanted to keep Bavaria as Catholic and an independent state. Nowadays, aside from the minority <a href="/wiki/Bavaria_Party" title="Bavaria Party">Bavaria Party</a>, most Bavarians accept that Bavaria is part of Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Another consideration is that Bavarians foster different cultural identities: <a href="/wiki/Franconia" title="Franconia">Franconia</a> in the north, speaking <a href="/wiki/East_Franconian_German" title="East Franconian German">East Franconian German</a>; Bavarian Swabia in the south west, speaking <a href="/wiki/Swabian_German" title="Swabian German">Swabian German</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Altbayern" title="Altbayern">Altbayern</a> (so-called "Old Bavaria", the regions forming the "historic", pentagon-shaped Bavaria before the acquisitions through the Vienna Congress, at present the districts of the Upper Palatinate, Lower and Upper Bavaria) speaking <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_language" title="Bavarian language">Austro-Bavarian</a>. In Munich, the Old Bavarian dialect was widely spread, but nowadays <a href="/wiki/High_German_languages" title="High German languages">High German</a> is predominantly spoken there. Moreover, by the <a href="/wiki/Flight_and_expulsion_of_Germans_(1944%E2%80%9350)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight and expulsion of Germans (1944–50)">expulsion of German speakers from Eastern Europe</a>, Bavaria has received a large population that was not traditionally Bavarian. In particular, the <a href="/wiki/Sudeten_Germans" title="Sudeten Germans">Sudeten Germans</a>, expelled from neighboring <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, have been deemed to have become the "fourth tribe" of Bavarians.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flags_and_coat_of_arms">Flags and coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Flags and coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Bavaria" title="Flag of Bavaria">Flag of Bavaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Bavaria" title="Coat of arms of Bavaria">Coat of arms of Bavaria</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flags">Flags</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Flags">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Bavaria_(lozengy).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_Bavaria_%28lozengy%29.svg/200px-Flag_of_Bavaria_%28lozengy%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_Bavaria_%28lozengy%29.svg/300px-Flag_of_Bavaria_%28lozengy%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_Bavaria_%28lozengy%29.svg/400px-Flag_of_Bavaria_%28lozengy%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Bavaria_(lozengy).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Second official flag of Bavaria</div></div></div>
<p>Uniquely among German states, Bavaria has two official flags of equal status, one with a white and blue stripe, the other with white and blue <a href="/wiki/Lozenge_(heraldry)" title="Lozenge (heraldry)">lozenges</a>. Either may be used by civilians and government offices, who are free to choose between them.<sup id="cite_ref-fotw_54_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fotw_54-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Unofficial versions of the flag, especially a lozenge style with coat of arms, are sometimes used by civilians.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Bavaria.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Coat_of_arms_of_Bavaria.svg/220px-Coat_of_arms_of_Bavaria.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Coat_of_arms_of_Bavaria.svg/330px-Coat_of_arms_of_Bavaria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Coat_of_arms_of_Bavaria.svg/440px-Coat_of_arms_of_Bavaria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="712" data-file-height="431" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Bavaria.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bavarian coat of arms</div></div></div>
<p>The modern coat of arms of Bavaria was designed by Eduard Ege in 1946, following heraldic traditions.
</p>
<ul><li>The Golden Lion: At the dexter chief, sable, a <a href="/wiki/Lion_(heraldry)" title="Lion (heraldry)">lion</a> rampant Or, armed and langued gules. This represents the administrative region of Upper Palatinate.</li>
<li>The "<a href="/wiki/Franconian_Rake" title="Franconian Rake">Franconian Rake</a>": At the sinister chief, per <a href="/wiki/Fess" title="Fess">fess</a> dancetty, gules, and argent. This represents the administrative regions of Upper, Middle and Lower Franconia.</li>
<li>The Blue "Pantier" (mythical creature from <a href="/wiki/French_heraldry" title="French heraldry">French heraldry</a>, sporting a flame instead of a tongue): At the dexter base, argent, a Pantier rampant azure, armed Or and langued gules. This represents the regions of Lower and Upper Bavaria.</li>
<li>The Three Lions: At the sinister base, Or, three lions passant guardant sable, armed and langued gules. This represents Swabia.</li>
<li>The White-And-Blue inescutcheon: The <a href="/wiki/Escutcheon_(heraldry)" title="Escutcheon (heraldry)">inescutcheon</a> of white and blue fusils askance was originally the coat of arms of the Counts of Bogen, adopted in 1247 by the House of Wittelsbach. The white-and-blue fusils are indisputably the emblem of Bavaria and these arms today symbolize Bavaria as a whole. Along with the People's Crown, it is officially used as the Minor Coat of Arms.</li>
<li>The People's Crown (<i>Volkskrone</i>): The coat of arms is surmounted by a <a href="/wiki/Crown_(heraldry)" title="Crown (heraldry)">crown</a> with a golden band inset with precious stones and decorated with five ornamental leaves. This crown first appeared in the coat of arms to symbolize sovereignty of <a href="/wiki/Common_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Common people">the people</a> after the royal crown was eschewed in 1923.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Cber_dem_Spitzsteinhaus_(3650068382).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/%C3%9Cber_dem_Spitzsteinhaus_%283650068382%29.jpg/220px-%C3%9Cber_dem_Spitzsteinhaus_%283650068382%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/%C3%9Cber_dem_Spitzsteinhaus_%283650068382%29.jpg/330px-%C3%9Cber_dem_Spitzsteinhaus_%283650068382%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/%C3%9Cber_dem_Spitzsteinhaus_%283650068382%29.jpg/440px-%C3%9Cber_dem_Spitzsteinhaus_%283650068382%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4224" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Cber_dem_Spitzsteinhaus_(3650068382).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bavarian Alps</div></div></div>
<p>Bavaria shares international borders with <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> (<a href="/wiki/Salzburg_(state)" title="Salzburg (state)">Salzburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyrol_(state)" title="Tyrol (state)">Tyrol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Upper_Austria" title="Upper Austria">Upper Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vorarlberg" title="Vorarlberg">Vorarlberg</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> (<a href="/wiki/Karlovy_Vary_Region" title="Karlovy Vary Region">Karlovy Vary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plze%C5%88_Region" title="Plzeň Region">Plzeň</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Bohemian_Region" title="South Bohemian Region">South Bohemian Regions</a>), as well as with <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (across <a href="/wiki/Lake_Constance" title="Lake Constance">Lake Constance</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_St._Gallen" title="Canton of St. Gallen">Canton of St. Gallen</a>). Because all of these countries are part of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, except for Switzerland, the border is completely open. Neighboring states within Germany are <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, Hesse, <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">Saxony</a>. Two major rivers flow through the state: the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> (<i>Donau</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Alps" title="Bavarian Alps">Bavarian Alps</a> define the border with Austria (including the Austrian federal-states of Vorarlberg, Tyrol and Salzburg), and within the range is the highest peak in Germany: the <a href="/wiki/Zugspitze" title="Zugspitze">Zugspitze</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Forest" title="Bavarian Forest">Bavarian Forest</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Forest" title="Bohemian Forest">Bohemian Forest</a> form the vast majority of the frontier with the Czech Republic and Bohemia.
</p><p>The major cities in Bavaria are <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> (<i>München</i>), <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a> (<i>Nürnberg</i>), <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regensburg" title="Regensburg">Regensburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ingolstadt" title="Ingolstadt">Ingolstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCrth" title="Fürth">Fürth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Erlangen" title="Erlangen">Erlangen</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Geographical_midpoint_of_Europe#Geographic_center_of_the_European_Union" title="Geographical midpoint of Europe">geographic center of the European Union</a> is located in the northwestern corner of Bavaria.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WV-Bavaria_regions.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/WV-Bavaria_regions.svg/220px-WV-Bavaria_regions.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/WV-Bavaria_regions.svg/330px-WV-Bavaria_regions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/WV-Bavaria_regions.svg/440px-WV-Bavaria_regions.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="917" data-file-height="889" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WV-Bavaria_regions.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Administrative districts (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Regierungsbezirke</i></i> and <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Bezirke</i></i>) of Bavaria</div></div></div>
<p>Bavaria is divided into seven administrative districts called <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Regierungsbezirke</i></i> (singular <i><i lang="de" title="German language text"><a href="/wiki/Regierungsbezirk" title="Regierungsbezirk">Regierungsbezirk</a></i></i>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_districts">Administrative districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Altbayern" title="Altbayern">Altbayern</a></b>:</li></ul>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Upper_Palatinate" title="Upper Palatinate">Upper Palatinate</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Oberpfalz</i></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Upper_Bavaria" title="Upper Bavaria">Upper Bavaria</a> (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Oberbayern</i></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lower_Bavaria" title="Lower Bavaria">Lower Bavaria</a> (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Niederbayern</i></i>)</li></ol>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Franconia" title="Franconia">Franconia</a></b>:</li></ul>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Upper_Franconia" title="Upper Franconia">Upper Franconia</a> (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Oberfranken</i></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Middle_Franconia" title="Middle Franconia">Middle Franconia</a> (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Mittelfranken</i></i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lower_Franconia" title="Lower Franconia">Lower Franconia</a> (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Unterfranken</i></i>)</li></ol>
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabia</a></b>:</li></ul>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Swabia_(administrative_region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Swabia (administrative region)">Swabia</a> (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Schwaben</i></i>)</li></ol>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts">Districts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Districts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Bezirke</i></i> (districts) are the third communal layer in Bavaria; the others are the <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Landkreise</i></i> and the <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Gemeinden</i></i> or <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Städte</i></i>. The <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Bezirke</i></i> in Bavaria are territorially identical with the <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Regierungsbezirke</i></i>, but they are self-governing regional corporation, having their own parliaments. In the other larger states of Germany, there are <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Regierungsbezirke</i></i> which are only administrative divisions and not self-governing entities as the <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Bezirke</i></i> in Bavaria.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Counties">Counties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Counties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The second communal layer is made up of 71 rural districts (called <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Landkreise</i></i>, singular <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Landkreis</i></i>) that are comparable to counties, as well as the 25 independent cities (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Kreisfreie Städte</i></i>, singular <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Kreisfreie Stadt</i></i>), both of which share the same administrative responsibilities .
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:435px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bavaria,_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bavaria%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg/433px-Bavaria%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg.png" decoding="async" width="433" height="427" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bavaria%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg/650px-Bavaria%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Bavaria%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg/866px-Bavaria%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="867" data-file-height="855" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bavaria,_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the <i>Landkreise</i> of Bavaria</div></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">Municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Municipalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 71 administrative districts are on the lowest level divided into 2,031 regular municipalities (called <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Gemeinden</i></i>, singular <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Gemeinde</i></i>). Together with the 25 independent cities (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">kreisfreie Städte</i></i>, which are in effect municipalities independent of <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Landkreis</i></i> administrations), there are a total of 2,056 municipalities in Bavaria.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frauenkirche_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Frauenkirche_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/220px-Frauenkirche_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Frauenkirche_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/330px-Frauenkirche_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Frauenkirche_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/440px-Frauenkirche_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2640" data-file-height="1760" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frauenkirche_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:N%C3%BCrnberger_Burg_im_Herbst_von_S%C3%BCdWest_05.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/N%C3%BCrnberger_Burg_im_Herbst_von_S%C3%BCdWest_05.JPG/220px-N%C3%BCrnberger_Burg_im_Herbst_von_S%C3%BCdWest_05.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/N%C3%BCrnberger_Burg_im_Herbst_von_S%C3%BCdWest_05.JPG/330px-N%C3%BCrnberger_Burg_im_Herbst_von_S%C3%BCdWest_05.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/N%C3%BCrnberger_Burg_im_Herbst_von_S%C3%BCdWest_05.JPG/440px-N%C3%BCrnberger_Burg_im_Herbst_von_S%C3%BCdWest_05.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:N%C3%BCrnberger_Burg_im_Herbst_von_S%C3%BCdWest_05.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a></div></div></div> 
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulrichsplatz_in_Augsburg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Ulrichsplatz_in_Augsburg.jpg/220px-Ulrichsplatz_in_Augsburg.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Ulrichsplatz_in_Augsburg.jpg/330px-Ulrichsplatz_in_Augsburg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Ulrichsplatz_in_Augsburg.jpg/440px-Ulrichsplatz_in_Augsburg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3406" data-file-height="2197" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ulrichsplatz_in_Augsburg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg_08_2006_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Regensburg_08_2006_2.jpg/220px-Regensburg_08_2006_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Regensburg_08_2006_2.jpg/330px-Regensburg_08_2006_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Regensburg_08_2006_2.jpg/440px-Regensburg_08_2006_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1501" data-file-height="1001" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regensburg_08_2006_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Regensburg" title="Regensburg">Regensburg</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 44 of the 71 administrative districts, there are a total of 215 <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated areas</a> (as of 1 January 2005, called <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">gemeindefreie Gebiete</i></i>, singular <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">gemeindefreies Gebiet</i></i>), not belonging to any municipality, all uninhabited, mostly forested areas, but also four lakes (<i lang="de" title="German language text"><a href="/wiki/Chiemsee" title="Chiemsee">Chiemsee</a></i>-without islands, <i lang="de" title="German language text"><a href="/wiki/Starnberger_See" class="mw-redirect" title="Starnberger See">Starnberger See</a></i>-without island <i lang="de" title="German language text">Roseninsel</i>, <i lang="de" title="German language text"><a href="/wiki/Ammersee" title="Ammersee">Ammersee</a></i>, which are the three largest lakes of Bavaria, and <i lang="de" title="German language text"><a href="/wiki/Waginger_See" title="Waginger See">Waginger See</a></i>).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayerische_Staatskanzlei_Munich_2014_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bayerische_Staatskanzlei_Munich_2014_02.jpg/220px-Bayerische_Staatskanzlei_Munich_2014_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bayerische_Staatskanzlei_Munich_2014_02.jpg/330px-Bayerische_Staatskanzlei_Munich_2014_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Bayerische_Staatskanzlei_Munich_2014_02.jpg/440px-Bayerische_Staatskanzlei_Munich_2014_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3400" data-file-height="2328" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayerische_Staatskanzlei_Munich_2014_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bayerische_Staatskanzlei" title="Bayerische Staatskanzlei">Bavarian State Chancellery</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bavaria" title="Politics of Bavaria">Politics of Bavaria</a></div>
<p>Bavaria has a multiparty system dominated by the conservative <a href="/wiki/Christian_Social_Union_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Social Union of Bavaria">Christian Social Union</a> (CSU), which has won every election since 1945, The Greens, which became the second biggest political party in the 2018 parliament elections and the center-left <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democrats</a> (SPD), which dominates in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>. Thus far <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Hoegner" title="Wilhelm Hoegner">Wilhelm Hoegner</a> has been the only SPD candidate to ever become Minister-President; notable successors in office include multi-term Federal Minister <a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Strauss" title="Franz Josef Strauss">Franz Josef Strauss</a>, a key figure among <a href="/wiki/West_German" class="mw-redirect" title="West German">West German</a> conservatives during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> years, and <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Stoiber" title="Edmund Stoiber">Edmund Stoiber</a>, who both failed with their bids for <a href="/wiki/Federal_Chancellor_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Chancellor of Germany">Chancellorship</a>. The German <a href="/wiki/Alliance_90/The_Greens" title="Alliance 90/The Greens">Greens</a> and the center-right <a href="/wiki/Free_Voters_of_Bavaria" title="Free Voters of Bavaria">Free Voters</a> have been represented in the state parliament since 1986 and 2008 respectively.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Bavaria_state_election,_2003" class="mw-redirect" title="Bavaria state election, 2003">2003 elections</a> the CSU won a <a href="/wiki/Supermajority" title="Supermajority">⅔ supermajority</a> – something no party had ever achieved in postwar Germany. However, in the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Bavaria_state_election,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Bavaria state election, 2008">2008 elections</a> the CSU lost the absolute majority for the first time in 46 years.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The losses were partly attributed by some to the CSU's stance for an anti-smoking bill.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag needs further explanation. (July 2018)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> (A first anti-smoking law had been proposed by the CSU and passed but was watered down after the election, after which a referendum enforced a strict antismoking bill with a large majority).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_Landtag">Current Landtag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Current Landtag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bavarian_Landtag_2018.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bavarian_Landtag_2018.svg/220px-Bavarian_Landtag_2018.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bavarian_Landtag_2018.svg/330px-Bavarian_Landtag_2018.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bavarian_Landtag_2018.svg/440px-Bavarian_Landtag_2018.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="185" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bavarian_Landtag_2018.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Current composition of the Landtag:<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #EB001F; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;SPD: 22 seats</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #64A12D; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;The Greens: 38 seats</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFED00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;FDP: 11 seats</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #007E82; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Free Voters: 27 seats</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:#008AC5; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;CSU: 85 seats</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #009EE0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;AfD: 22 seats</div></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_state_election,_2018" class="mw-redirect" title="Bavarian state election, 2018">last state elections</a> were held on 14 October 2018 in which the CSU lost its absolute majority in the state parliament in part due to the party's stances as part of the federal government, winning 37.2% of the vote; the party's second worst election outcome in its history. The Greens who had surged in the polls leading up to the election have replaced the social-democratic SPD as the second biggest force in the <a href="/wiki/Landtag_of_Bavaria" title="Landtag of Bavaria">Landtag</a> with 17.5% of the vote. The SPD lost over half of its previous share compared to 2013 with a mere 9.7% in 2018. The liberals of the FDP were again able to reach the five-percent-threshold in order to receive mandates in parliament after they were not part of the <i>Landtag</i> after the 2013 elections. Also entering the new parliament will be the right-wing populist Alternative for Germany (AfD) with 10.2% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The center-right Free Voters party gained 11.6% of the vote and formed a government coalition with the CSU which lead to the subsequent reelection of Markus Söder as <a href="/wiki/Minister-President_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister-President of Bavaria">Minister-President of Bavaria</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bavaria" title="Constitution of Bavaria">Constitution of Bavaria</a> of the Free State of Bavaria was enacted on 8 December 1946. The new Bavarian Constitution became the basis for the Bavarian State after the Second World War.
</p><p>Bavaria has a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> <i><i lang="de" title="German language text"><a href="/wiki/Landtag_of_Bavaria" title="Landtag of Bavaria">Landtag</a></i></i> (English: State Parliament), elected by universal suffrage. Until December 1999, there was also a <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Senat</i></i>, or <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Senate" title="Bavarian Senate">Senate</a>, whose members were chosen by social and economic groups in Bavaria, but following a referendum in 1998, this institution was abolished.
</p><p>The Bavarian State Government consists of the <a href="/wiki/Minister-President_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister-President of Bavaria">Minister-President of Bavaria</a>, eleven Ministers and six Secretaries of State. The Minister-President is elected for a period of five years by the State Parliament and is head of state. With the approval of the State Parliament he appoints the members of the State Government. The State Government is composed of the:
</p>
<ul><li>Ministry of the Interior, Building and Transport (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Staatsministerium des Innern, für Bau und Verkehr</i></i>)</li>
<li>Ministry of Education and Culture, Science and Art (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Staatsministerium für Bildung und Kultus, Wissenschaft und Kunst</i></i>)</li>
<li>Ministry of Finance, for Rural Development and Homeland (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Staatsministerium der Finanzen, für Landesentwicklung und Heimat</i></i>)</li>
<li>Ministry of Economic Affairs and Media, Energy and Technology (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Staatsministerium für Wirtschaft und Medien, Energie und Technologie</i></i>)</li>
<li>Ministry of Environment and Consumer Protection (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Staatsministerium für Umwelt und Verbraucherschutz</i></i>)</li>
<li>Ministry of Labour and Social Affairs, Family and Integration (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Staatsministerium für Arbeit und Soziales, Familie und Integration</i></i>)</li>
<li>Ministry of Justice (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Staatsministerium der Justiz</i></i>)</li>
<li>Ministry of Food, Agriculture and Forestry (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Staatsministerium für Ernährung, Landwirtschaft und Forsten</i></i>)</li>
<li>Ministry of Public Health and Care Services (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Staatsministerium für Gesundheit und Pflege</i></i>)</li></ul>
<p>Political processes also take place in the seven regions (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Regierungsbezirke</i></i> or <i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Bezirke</i></i>) in Bavaria, in the 71 administrative districts (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Landkreise</i></i>) and the 25 towns and cities forming their own districts (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">kreisfreie Städte</i></i>), and in the 2,031 local authorities (<i><i lang="de" title="German language text">Gemeinden</i></i>).
</p><p>In 1995 Bavaria introduced <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct democracy</a> on the local level in a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a>. This was initiated bottom-up by an association called <i>Mehr Demokratie</i> (English: More Democracy). This is a grass-roots organization which campaigns for the right to citizen-initiated referendums. In 1997 the Bavarian Supreme Court tightened the regulations considerably (including by introducing a turn-out quorum). Nevertheless, Bavaria has the most advanced regulations on local direct democracy in Germany. This has led to a spirited citizens' participation in communal and municipal affairs—835 referenda took place from 1995 through 2005.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Minister-presidents_of_Bavaria_since_1945">Minister-presidents of Bavaria since 1945</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Minister-presidents of Bavaria since 1945">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
