<h3><span id="Designation_as_a_.22free_state.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Designation_as_a_&quot;free_state&quot;">Designation as a "free state"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Designation as a &quot;free state&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Unlike most German states (<i>Länder</i>), which simply designate themselves as "State of" (<i>Land [...]</i>), Bavaria uses the style of "Free State of Bavaria" (<i>Freistaat Bayern</i>). The difference from other states is purely terminological, as German constitutional law does not draw a distinction between "States" and "Free States". The situation is thus analogous to the United States, where <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">some states</a> use the style "Commonwealth" rather than "State". The choice of "Free State", a creation of the early 20th century and intended to be a German alternative to (or translation of) the Latin-derived "republic", has historical reasons, Bavaria having been styled that way even before the current 1946 Constitution was enacted (in 1918 after the de facto abdication of Ludwig III). Two other states, <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">Saxony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a>, also use the style "Free State"; unlike Bavaria, however, these were not part of the original states when the <a href="/wiki/Grundgesetz" class="mw-redirect" title="Grundgesetz">Grundgesetz</a> was enacted but joined the federation later on, in 1990, as a result of <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a>. Saxony had used the designation as "Free State" from 1918 to 1952.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arbitrary_arrest_and_human_rights">Arbitrary arrest and human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Arbitrary arrest and human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2017, Bavaria's parliament enacted a new revision of the "Gefährdergesetz", allowing the authorities to imprison a person for a three months term, renewable indefinitely, when he or she has not committed a crime but it is assumed that he or she might commit a crime "in the near future".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Critics like the prominent journalist <a href="/wiki/Heribert_Prantl" title="Heribert Prantl">Heribert Prantl</a> have called the law "shameful" and compared it to <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_detention_camp" title="Guantanamo Bay detention camp">Guantanamo Bay detention camp</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> assessed it to be in violation of the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> and also compared it to the legal situation in Russia, where a similar law allows for imprisonment for a maximum term of two years (i.e., not indefinitely)<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BMW_Welt_y_Torre_BMW,_M%C3%BAnich,_Alemania,_2015-07-03,_DD_25-27_HDR.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/BMW_Welt_y_Torre_BMW%2C_M%C3%BAnich%2C_Alemania%2C_2015-07-03%2C_DD_25-27_HDR.JPG/220px-BMW_Welt_y_Torre_BMW%2C_M%C3%BAnich%2C_Alemania%2C_2015-07-03%2C_DD_25-27_HDR.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/BMW_Welt_y_Torre_BMW%2C_M%C3%BAnich%2C_Alemania%2C_2015-07-03%2C_DD_25-27_HDR.JPG/330px-BMW_Welt_y_Torre_BMW%2C_M%C3%BAnich%2C_Alemania%2C_2015-07-03%2C_DD_25-27_HDR.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/BMW_Welt_y_Torre_BMW%2C_M%C3%BAnich%2C_Alemania%2C_2015-07-03%2C_DD_25-27_HDR.JPG/440px-BMW_Welt_y_Torre_BMW%2C_M%C3%BAnich%2C_Alemania%2C_2015-07-03%2C_DD_25-27_HDR.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6970" data-file-height="3077" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BMW_Welt_y_Torre_BMW,_M%C3%BAnich,_Alemania,_2015-07-03,_DD_25-27_HDR.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/BMW_Welt" title="BMW Welt">BMW Welt</a> and <a href="/wiki/BMW_Headquarters" title="BMW Headquarters">BMW Headquarters</a> in Munich</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Neuschwanstein_Castle_LOC_print_rotated.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Neuschwanstein_Castle_LOC_print_rotated.jpg/220px-Neuschwanstein_Castle_LOC_print_rotated.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Neuschwanstein_Castle_LOC_print_rotated.jpg/330px-Neuschwanstein_Castle_LOC_print_rotated.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Neuschwanstein_Castle_LOC_print_rotated.jpg/440px-Neuschwanstein_Castle_LOC_print_rotated.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3502" data-file-height="2554" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Neuschwanstein_Castle_LOC_print_rotated.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Neuschwanstein_Castle" title="Neuschwanstein Castle">Neuschwanstein Castle</a> (pictured) and <a href="/wiki/Hohenschwangau_Castle" title="Hohenschwangau Castle">Hohenschwangau Castle</a> draw many tourists to the region annually.</div></div></div>
<p>Bavaria has long had one of the largest economies of any region in Germany, and in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Its GDP in 2007 exceeded €434&#160;billion (about U.S. $600&#160;billion).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> This makes Bavaria itself one of the largest economies in Europe, and only 20 countries in the world have a higher GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Large companies headquartered in Bavaria include <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rohde_%26_Schwarz" title="Rohde &amp; Schwarz">Rohde &amp; Schwarz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a>, <a href="/wiki/MTU_Aero_Engines" title="MTU Aero Engines">MTU Aero Engines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munich_Re" title="Munich Re">Munich Re</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">Allianz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Infineon" class="mw-redirect" title="Infineon">Infineon</a>, <a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">MAN SE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wacker_Chemie" title="Wacker Chemie">Wacker Chemie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puma_SE" class="mw-redirect" title="Puma SE">Puma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ruf_Automobile" title="Ruf Automobile">Ruf</a>. Bavaria has a GDP per capita of over U.S. $48,000; if it were an independent country it would rank 7th or 8th<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> in the world. Bavaria has strong economic ties with Austria, the Czech Republic, Switzerland, and Northern Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Companies">Companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The motorcycle and automobile maker BMW <i>Bayerische Motoren-Werke</i>, or Bavarian Motor Works in English, Audi, Allianz, <a href="/wiki/Grundig" title="Grundig">Grundig</a> (consumer electronics), Siemens (electricity, telephones, informatics, medical instruments), <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a>, Weltbild (trade) <a href="/wiki/Patrizia_Immobilien" title="Patrizia Immobilien">Patrizia Immobilien</a> (real estate management) <a href="/wiki/Continental_AG" title="Continental AG">Continental</a> (automotive tires and electronics), <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a>, Adidas, <a href="/wiki/Puma_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Puma AG">Puma</a>, HypoVereinsbank (UniCredit Group), Infineon, <a href="/wiki/Krauss-Maffei" title="Krauss-Maffei">Krauss-Maffei Wegmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/MAN_Diesel_%26_Turbo" class="mw-redirect" title="MAN Diesel &amp; Turbo">MAN Diesel &amp; Turbo</a>, <a href="/wiki/KUKA" title="KUKA">KUKA</a>, <a href="/wiki/OSRAM" class="mw-redirect" title="OSRAM">OSRAM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruf_Automobile" title="Ruf Automobile">Ruf</a> have (or had) a Bavarian industrial base.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unemployment">Unemployment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Unemployment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The unemployment rate stood at 2.6% in October 2018, the lowest in Germany and one of the lowest in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pop_density_of_Germany.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Pop_density_of_Germany.png/220px-Pop_density_of_Germany.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Pop_density_of_Germany.png/330px-Pop_density_of_Germany.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Pop_density_of_Germany.png/440px-Pop_density_of_Germany.png 2x" data-file-width="817" data-file-height="1019" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pop_density_of_Germany.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bavaria is one of Germany's least densely populated states</div></div></div>
<p>Bavaria has a population of approximately 12.9&#160;million inhabitants (2016). 8 of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_with_more_than_100,000_inhabitants" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Germany with more than 100,000 inhabitants">80 largest cities in Germany</a> are located within Bavaria with Munich being the largest (1,450,381 inhabitants, approximately 5.7&#160;million when including the broader metropolitan area), followed by <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a> (509,975 inhabitants) and <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a> (286,374 inhabitants). All other cities in Bavaria had less than 150,000 inhabitants each in 2015. Population density in Bavaria was 182 inhabitants per square kilometre (470/sq&#160;mi), below the national average of 227 inhabitants per square kilometre (590/sq&#160;mi). Foreign nationals resident in Bavaria (both <a href="/wiki/Immigrants" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrants">immigrants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Refugees" class="mw-redirect" title="Refugees">refugees</a>/<a href="/wiki/Asylum_seekers" class="mw-redirect" title="Asylum seekers">asylum seekers</a>) were principally from other EU countries and Turkey.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vital_statistics">Vital statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Vital statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-List_to_table plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This list (which may have dates, numbers, etc.) <b>may be better in a <a href="/wiki/Help:Sorting" title="Help:Sorting">sortable table</a> format.</b><span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit">improve this list</a> or discuss it on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Bavaria" title="Talk:Bavaria">talk page</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2019</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>

</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Some features of the Bavarian culture and mentality are remarkably distinct from the rest of Germany. Noteworthy differences (especially in rural areas, less significant in the major cities) can be found with respect to religion, traditions, and language.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baroque_Church_of_Saint-Coloman_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Baroque_Church_of_Saint-Coloman_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Baroque_Church_of_Saint-Coloman_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Baroque_Church_of_Saint-Coloman_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Baroque_Church_of_Saint-Coloman_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Baroque_Church_of_Saint-Coloman_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Baroque_Church_of_Saint-Coloman_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baroque_Church_of_Saint-Coloman_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Catholic church near <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCssen" title="Füssen">Füssen</a> with the Alps in the background</div></div></div>
<p>Bavarian culture (<i><a href="/wiki/Altbayern" title="Altbayern">Altbayern</a></i>) has a long and predominant tradition of <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> faith. Pope emeritus <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Benedict XVI (Joseph Alois Ratzinger)</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Marktl_am_Inn" class="mw-redirect" title="Marktl am Inn">Marktl am Inn</a> in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Bavaria" title="Upper Bavaria">Upper Bavaria</a> and was <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Munich_and_Freising" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishop of Munich and Freising">Cardinal-Archbishop of Munich and Freising</a>. Otherwise, the culturally <a href="/wiki/Franconia" title="Franconia">Franconian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabian</a> regions of the modern State of Bavaria are historically more diverse in religiosity, with both Catholic and <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> traditions. In 1925, 70.0% of the Bavarian population was <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>, 28.8% was <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, 0.7% was <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a>, and 0.5% was placed in other religious categories.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> 49.6% of Bavarians adhered to Catholicism (a decline from 70.4% in 1970).<sup id="cite_ref-BR_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BR-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EKD2017_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EKD2017-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> 18.3% of the population adheres to the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_Bavaria" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in Bavaria">Evangelical Lutheran Church in Bavaria</a>, which has also declined since 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-BR_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BR-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EKD2017_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EKD2017-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> 3% was <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> make up 4.0% of the population of Bavaria. 28.1% of Bavarians are irreligious or adhere to other religions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bavarians commonly emphasize pride in their traditions. Traditional costumes collectively known as <a href="/wiki/Tracht" title="Tracht">Tracht</a> are worn on special occasions and include in <a href="/wiki/Altbayern" title="Altbayern">Altbayern</a> <a href="/wiki/Lederhosen" title="Lederhosen">Lederhosen</a> for males and <a href="/wiki/Dirndl" title="Dirndl">Dirndl</a> for females. Centuries-old <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> is performed. The <a href="/wiki/Maypole_tradition_in_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Maypole tradition in Bavaria">Maibaum</a>, or Maypole (which in the Middle Ages served as the community's business directory, as figures on the pole represented the trades of the village), and the bagpipes of the Upper Palatinate region bear witness to the <a href="/wiki/Paganism_in_the_Eastern_Alps" class="mw-redirect" title="Paganism in the Eastern Alps">ancient Celtic and Germanic</a> remnants of cultural heritage of the region. There are many traditional Bavarian sports disciplines, e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Aperschnalzen" title="Aperschnalzen">Aperschnalzen</a>, competitive <a href="/wiki/Whipcracking" title="Whipcracking">whipcracking</a>.
</p><p>Whether actually in Bavaria, overseas or with citizens from other nations Bavarians continue to cultivate their traditions. They hold festivals and dances to keep their heritage alive. In New York City the German American Cultural Society is a larger umbrella group for others which represent a specific part of Germany, including the Bavarian organizations. They present a German parade called <a href="/wiki/Steuben_Parade" class="mw-redirect" title="Steuben Parade">Steuben Parade</a> each year. Various affiliated events take place amongst its groups, one of which is the Bavarian Dancers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_drink">Food and drink</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Food and drink">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bavarians tend to place a great value on <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_cuisine" title="Bavarian cuisine">food and drink</a>. In addition to their renowned dishes, Bavarians also consume many items of food and drink which are unusual elsewhere in Germany; for example <i lang="de" title="German language text"><a href="/wiki/Wei%C3%9Fwurst" class="mw-redirect" title="Weißwurst">Weißwurst</a></i> ("white sausage") or in some instances a variety of entrails. At folk festivals and in many <a href="/wiki/Beer_garden" title="Beer garden">beer gardens</a>, beer is traditionally served by the litre (in a <i lang="de" title="German language text"><a href="/wiki/Ma%C3%9F" title="Maß">Maß</a></i>). Bavarians are particularly proud<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> of the traditional <i lang="de" title="German language text"><a href="/wiki/Reinheitsgebot" title="Reinheitsgebot">Reinheitsgebot</a></i>, or beer purity law, initially established by the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Bavaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Bavaria">Duke of Bavaria</a> for the City of Munich (i.e. the court) in 1487 and the duchy in 1516. According to this law, only three ingredients were allowed in beer: water, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hops" title="Hops">hops</a>. In 1906 the <i lang="de" title="German language text">Reinheitsgebot</i> made its way to all-German law, and remained a law in Germany until the EU partly struck it down in 1987 as incompatible with the European common market.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> German breweries, however, cling to the principle, and Bavarian breweries still comply with it in order to distinguish their beer brands.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Bavarians are also known as some of the world's most beer-loving people with an average annual consumption of 170 liters per person, although figures have been declining in recent years.
</p><p>Bavaria is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Franconia_(wine_region)" title="Franconia (wine region)">Franconia wine region</a>, which is situated along the <a href="/wiki/Main_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Main River">Main River</a> in Franconia. The region has produced wine (<i>Frankenwein</i>) for over 1,000 years and is famous for its use of the <a href="/wiki/Bocksbeutel" title="Bocksbeutel">Bocksbeutel</a> wine bottle. The production of wine forms an integral part of the regional culture, and many of its villages and cities hold their own wine festivals (Weinfeste) throughout the year.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language_and_dialects">Language and dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Language and dialects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oberdeutsche_Mundarten.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Oberdeutsche_Mundarten.png/150px-Oberdeutsche_Mundarten.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Oberdeutsche_Mundarten.png/225px-Oberdeutsche_Mundarten.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Oberdeutsche_Mundarten.png/300px-Oberdeutsche_Mundarten.png 2x" data-file-width="745" data-file-height="1053" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oberdeutsche_Mundarten.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Upper German, southern counterpart to Central German, both forming the High German Languages. Blue are the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_language" title="Bavarian language">Austro-Bavarian</a> dialects</div></div></div>
<p>Three German dialects are most commonly spoken in Bavaria: <a href="/wiki/Austro-Bavarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Bavarian">Austro-Bavarian</a> in Old Bavaria (Upper Bavaria, Lower Bavaria and the Upper Palatinate), <a href="/wiki/Swabian_German" title="Swabian German">Swabian German</a> (an <a href="/wiki/Alemannic_German" title="Alemannic German">Alemannic German</a> dialect) in the Bavarian part of Swabia (south west) and <a href="/wiki/East_Franconian_German" title="East Franconian German">East Franconian German</a> in Franconia (North). In the small town <a href="/wiki/Ludwigsstadt" title="Ludwigsstadt">Ludwigsstadt</a> in the north, district Kronach in Upper Franconia, <a href="/wiki/Thuringian_dialect" title="Thuringian dialect">Thuringian dialect</a> is spoken. During the 20th century an increasing part of the population began to speak <a href="/wiki/Standard_German" title="Standard German">Standard German</a> (Hochdeutsch), mainly in the cities.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnography">Ethnography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Ethnography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bavarians consider themselves to be <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarian</a> and informal.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Their sociability can be experienced at the annual <a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">Oktoberfest</a>, the world's largest beer festival, which welcomes around six million visitors every year, or in the famous <a href="/wiki/Beer_garden" title="Beer garden">beer gardens</a>. In traditional Bavarian beer gardens, patrons may bring their own food but buy beer only from the brewery that runs the beer garden.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In the United States, particularly among <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">German Americans</a>, Bavarian culture is viewed somewhat nostalgically, and several "Bavarian villages" have been founded, most notably <a href="/wiki/Frankenmuth,_Michigan" title="Frankenmuth, Michigan">Frankenmuth, Michigan</a>; <a href="/wiki/Helen,_Georgia" title="Helen, Georgia">Helen, Georgia</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Leavenworth,_Washington" title="Leavenworth, Washington">Leavenworth, Washington</a>. Since 1962, the latter has been styled with a Bavarian theme and is home to an Oktoberfest celebration it claims is among the most attended in the world outside of Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg/220px-Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="79" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg/330px-Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg/440px-Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5000" data-file-height="1786" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Allianz_arena_at_night_Richard_Bartz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a>, one of the world's most famous football stadiums</div></div></div>
<p>Bavaria is home to several football clubs including <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">FC Bayern Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">1. FC Nürnberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Augsburg" title="FC Augsburg">FC Augsburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/TSV_1860_Munich" title="TSV 1860 Munich">TSV 1860 Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Ingolstadt_04" title="FC Ingolstadt 04">FC Ingolstadt 04</a> and <a href="/wiki/SpVgg_Greuther_F%C3%BCrth" title="SpVgg Greuther Fürth">SpVgg Greuther Fürth</a>. Bayern Munich is the most popular and successful football team in Germany having won a record 27 German titles. They are followed by 1. FC Nürnberg who have won 9 titles. SpVgg Greuther Fürth have won 3 championships while TSV 1860 Munich have been champions once. FC Bayern won the <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_football_champions" title="List of German football champions">German championship</a> 27 times (record) and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> 5 times.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bavarians">Bavarians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bavaria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Bavarians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Many famous people have been born or lived in present-day Bavaria:
</p>
<ul><li><b>Kings</b>: <a href="/wiki/Arnulf_of_Carinthia" title="Arnulf of Carinthia">Arnulf of Carinthia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carloman_of_Bavaria" title="Carloman of Bavaria">Carloman of Bavaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Fat" title="Charles the Fat">Charles the Fat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lothair_I" title="Lothair I">Lothair I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Child" title="Louis the Child">Louis the Child</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_German" title="Louis the German">Louis the German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Younger" title="Louis the Younger">Louis the Younger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_I_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig I of Bavaria">Ludwig I of Bavaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_II_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig II of Bavaria">Ludwig II of Bavaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_III_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig III of Bavaria">Ludwig III of Bavaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I_Joseph_of_Bavaria" title="Maximilian I Joseph of Bavaria">Maximilian I Joseph of Bavaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_II_of_Bavaria" title="Maximilian II of Bavaria">Maximilian II of Bavaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otto_of_Bavaria" title="Otto of Bavaria">Otto of Bavaria</a></li>
<li><b>Religious leaders</b>: <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> (Joseph Aloisius Ratzinger); <a href="/wiki/Pope_Damasus_II" title="Pope Damasus II">Pope Damasus II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Victor_II" title="Pope Victor II">Pope Victor II</a>.</li>
<li><b>Painters</b>: <a href="/wiki/Hans_Holbein_the_Elder" title="Hans Holbein the Elder">Hans Holbein the Elder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer" title="Albrecht Dürer">Albrecht Dürer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_Altdorfer" title="Albrecht Altdorfer">Albrecht Altdorfer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Cranach_the_Elder" title="Lucas Cranach the Elder">Lucas Cranach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Spitzweg" title="Carl Spitzweg">Carl Spitzweg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Christian_Reinhart" title="Johann Christian Reinhart">Johann Christian Reinhart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_von_Lenbach" title="Franz von Lenbach">Franz von Lenbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Stuck" title="Franz Stuck">Franz von Stuck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Marc" title="Franz Marc">Franz Marc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Klee" title="Paul Klee">Paul Klee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Eisch" title="Erwin Eisch">Erwin Eisch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabriele_M%C3%BCnter" title="Gabriele Münter">Gabriele Münter</a>.</li>
<li><b>Classical musicians</b> <a href="/wiki/Orlande_de_Lassus" title="Orlande de Lassus">Orlando di Lasso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Willibald_Gluck" title="Christoph Willibald Gluck">Christoph Willibald Gluck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Mozart" title="Leopold Mozart">Leopold Mozart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Max_Reger" title="Max Reger">Max Reger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">Richard Wagner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Strauss" title="Richard Strauss">Richard Strauss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Orff" title="Carl Orff">Carl Orff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Pachelbel" title="Johann Pachelbel">Johann Pachelbel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theobald_Boehm" title="Theobald Boehm">Theobald Boehm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Nomi" title="Klaus Nomi">Klaus Nomi</a>.</li>
<li><b>Other musicians</b> <a href="/wiki/Hans-J%C3%BCrgen_Buchner" class="mw-redirect" title="Hans-Jürgen Buchner">Hans-Jürgen Buchner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Dennerlein" title="Barbara Dennerlein">Barbara Dennerlein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Doldinger" title="Klaus Doldinger">Klaus Doldinger</a>, Bands: <a href="/wiki/Spider_Murphy_Gang" title="Spider Murphy Gang">Spider Murphy Gang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sportfreunde_Stiller" title="Sportfreunde Stiller">Sportfreunde Stiller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obscura_(band)" title="Obscura (band)">Obscura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bredl" title="Michael Bredl">Michael Bredl</a></li>
<li><b>Opera singers</b> <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Kaufmann" title="Jonas Kaufmann">Jonas Kaufmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diana_Damrau" title="Diana Damrau">Diana Damrau</a>.</li>
<li><b>Writers</b>, <b>poets</b> and <b>playwrights</b> <a href="/wiki/Hans_Sachs" title="Hans Sachs">Hans Sachs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Paul" title="Jean Paul">Jean Paul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_R%C3%BCckert" title="Friedrich Rückert">Friedrich Rückert</a>, <a href="/wiki/August_von_Platen-Hallerm%C3%BCnde" title="August von Platen-Hallermünde">August von Platen-Hallermünde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Wedekind" title="Frank Wedekind">Frank Wedekind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Morgenstern" title="Christian Morgenstern">Christian Morgenstern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Maria_Graf" title="Oskar Maria Graf">Oskar Maria Graf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bertolt_Brecht" title="Bertolt Brecht">Bertolt Brecht</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lion_Feuchtwanger" title="Lion Feuchtwanger">Lion Feuchtwanger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mann" title="Thomas Mann">Thomas Mann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Mann" title="Klaus Mann">Klaus Mann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golo_Mann" title="Golo Mann">Golo Mann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Thoma" title="Ludwig Thoma">Ludwig Thoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ende" title="Michael Ende">Michael Ende</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Aurbacher" title="Ludwig Aurbacher">Ludwig Aurbacher</a>.</li>
<li><b>Scientists</b> <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck" title="Max Planck">Max Planck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Conrad_R%C3%B6ntgen" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen">Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Werner_Heisenberg" title="Werner Heisenberg">Werner Heisenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Ries" title="Adam Ries">Adam Ries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_von_Fraunhofer" title="Joseph von Fraunhofer">Joseph von Fraunhofer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georg_Ohm" title="Georg Ohm">Georg Ohm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Stark" title="Johannes Stark">Johannes Stark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_von_Linde" title="Carl von Linde">Carl von Linde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Prandtl" title="Ludwig Prandtl">Ludwig Prandtl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_M%C3%B6ssbauer" title="Rudolf Mössbauer">Rudolf Mössbauer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lothar_Rohde" class="mw-redirect" title="Lothar Rohde">Lothar Rohde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Schwarz" title="Hermann Schwarz">Hermann Schwarz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Huber" title="Robert Huber">Robert Huber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Behaim" title="Martin Behaim">Martin Behaim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Levi_Strauss" title="Levi Strauss">Levi Strauss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Diesel" title="Rudolf Diesel">Rudolf Diesel</a>.</li>
<li><b>Physicians</b> <a href="/wiki/Max_Joseph_von_Pettenkofer" title="Max Joseph von Pettenkofer">Max Joseph von Pettenkofer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Kneipp" title="Sebastian Kneipp">Sebastian Kneipp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alois_Alzheimer" title="Alois Alzheimer">Alois Alzheimer</a>.</li>
<li><b>Politicians</b> <a href="/wiki/Horst_Seehofer" title="Horst Seehofer">Horst Seehofer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Ude" title="Christian Ude">Christian Ude</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Eisner" title="Kurt Eisner">Kurt Eisner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz-Josef_Strau%C3%9F" class="mw-redirect" title="Franz-Josef Strauß">Franz-Josef Strauß</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Herzog" title="Roman Herzog">Roman Herzog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonard_John_Rose" title="Leonard John Rose">Leonard John Rose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kissinger" title="Henry Kissinger">Henry Kissinger</a>.</li>
<li><b>Football players</b> <a href="/wiki/Max_Morlock" title="Max Morlock">Max Morlock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Mai" title="Karl Mai">Karl Mai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Franz Beckenbauer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Maier" title="Sepp Maier">Sepp Maier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerd_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerd Müller">Gerd Müller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Breitner" title="Paul Breitner">Paul Breitner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bernd_Schuster" title="Bernd Schuster">Bernd Schuster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Augenthaler" title="Klaus Augenthaler">Klaus Augenthaler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lothar_Matth%C3%A4us" title="Lothar Matthäus">Lothar Matthäus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Lahm" title="Philipp Lahm">Philipp Lahm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bastian_Schweinsteiger" title="Bastian Schweinsteiger">Bastian Schweinsteiger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holger_Badstuber" title="Holger Badstuber">Holger Badstuber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_M%C3%BCller" title="Thomas Müller">Thomas Müller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mario_G%C3%B6tze" title="Mario Götze">Mario Götze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dietmar_Hamann" title="Dietmar Hamann">Dietmar Hamann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Reuter" title="Stefan Reuter">Stefan Reuter</a></li>
<li><b>Other sportspeople</b> <a href="/wiki/Bernhard_Langer" title="Bernhard Langer">Bernhard Langer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dirk_Nowitzki" title="Dirk Nowitzki">Dirk Nowitzki</a></li>
<li><b>Actors</b> <a href="/wiki/Werner_Stocker_(actor)" title="Werner Stocker (actor)">Werner Stocker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Fischer" title="Helmut Fischer">Helmut Fischer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Sedlmayr" title="Walter Sedlmayr">Walter Sedlmayr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustl_Bayrhammer" title="Gustl Bayrhammer">Gustl Bayrhammer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottfried_Fischer" title="Ottfried Fischer">Ottfried Fischer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Drexel" title="Ruth Drexel">Ruth Drexel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elmar_Wepper" title="Elmar Wepper">Elmar Wepper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Wepper" title="Fritz Wepper">Fritz Wepper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uschi_Glas" title="Uschi Glas">Uschi Glas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yank_Azman" title="Yank Azman">Yank Azman</a>.</li>

<li><b>Designers</b> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Schreyer" title="Peter Schreyer">Peter Schreyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damir_Doma" title="Damir Doma">Damir Doma</a></li>
